<name>David Good</name>< Rate>
4<//Rate>
< text>
Excellent experience!  Great atmosphere (one of the main reasons to come here) as you get to experience film in an older style setting, but with updated seats and amenities.  The second reason to come here is... the beer.  If you love to watch movies, but love those movies even more with a tasty beverage on hand... this is the place to go.  Shoot -- they even still have a balcony!!  How many new theaters today have a balcony?  So... the location is great (sans parking), the staff is great, and being able to sip on a beverage is certainly an added plus and makes even the worst flicks tolerable.  The one gripe I have about this place is that they don't really have any automation built into their ordering system. You basically have to fill out a large card (in the dark) stating what you want, and how much you want... and then you have to calculate the cost and insert the correct cash or a credit card.  You fold the card and stick it in a slot and wait for one of the staff members to notice... and that's the problem.  One night my brother-in-law and I waited for a half hour without any staff coming by, so we just made the trip downstairs ourselves.  On another visit, the staff was right on top of things and spotted the cards right away.  If they had a wireless "ringer" system (where you just punch a "call button" and the staff knows exactly where to go) it would run much smoother.  Until then, I can handle a few hit-or-misses since this is such a great place to watch movies.  Prices are great as well, which I can't say for other theaters.< /text>

< text>
Would be nice if it still felt like a movie theater instead of trying to be a hip college scene. Because of that the movies are an afterthought. "Drink beer, eat empanadas! And while you're at it, why not watch a movie?". An awesome old theater is done and gone. Sadly, they are often the only place around Humboldt showing lesser known movies. So sometimes I have to bite the bullet.

P.S. Don't sit near a door unless you want to hear it open and close endlessly throughout your movie.< /text>

<Rate>5<//Rate>< text>
The movie theater in Humboldt County!  The remodel has breathed new life into this historic building.  I can remember seeing movies here thirty years ago, but the experience and  seating was never this good!      The theaters have large, comfortable chairs with a long counter in front of each row to place your food, which can be ordered from your seats!  Just fill out the order forms,  place them on the counter in front of you with your credit card and an attendant comes by and fills you order.  The prices are reasonable, if not cheaper than other theaters, and this is the only movie theater around that will deliver pizza and beer directly to you seats!  We will be back for our next movie night, and can't imagine going anywhere else!</text>

<Text>I was sent a random text for an offer of 2 weeks free trial classes. When i accepted within 2 minutes of offer, i was directed to fill a questionnaire because spaces were limited. Part of the questionnaire was why i chose it's facilities, if i saw myself going a minimum of 2x a week, and if i saw myself spending $165 a month.
During this pandemic, not too many people can afford pricey memberships. So my current situation did not see myself enrolling after trials. But that did not mean i would not consider after.
After my responses, i was notified that the trials were not being offered and i would be placed on a wait list.
If that was an attempt to lure me in using a free trial offer, their plan not only failed, but it also cause an unpleasant welcoming.< /Text><userid>111965267625679338585</userid><Date>1605563008564<//Date>< rate>

<Text>10th Planet San Mateo is an awesome place to learn jiu jitsu, and is home to a great community of people.  It's a place where guys and girls from all walks of life come together to progress as grapplers and human beings.  I came in with no grappling experience, but quickly fell in love with jiu jitsu at this gym.  Training at 10th Planet San Mateo is now what I look forward to the most on a daily basis.  Beginners are eased in, and safety is a big priority.  Signing up for this gym was one of the best decisions I've ever made, and I'd highly recommend it to others.</Text>< Pictures>
[{'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipPzu7gFbaj3qD0JvpAkhkEmaY-Em1CcbgDbyJw9=w150-h150-k-no-p']}]<//Pictures>
<Response>None<//Response><gmapID>0x808f9ef9693b7505:0x52302808ccb127a1<//gmapID></record></dataset><record>
<userid>113120002077957443037</userid><Response>{'time': 1604382206555, 'text': 'Thanks for your critical feedback Cyrus. We are really sorry you feel this way. We believe we did our best to find a resolution and make you happy by refunding your payment from 2019. I hope you can find what you are looking for with the next gym you decide to train at.'}< /Response>< text>
TL;DR: 5 stars for community, -2 for management shadiness, -2 for safety (bjj + covid). For the full review, see yelp.

A strength of this gym is a large community of dedicated practitioners at a variety of belt levels. The instruction is also good. Alan Sanchez in particular is laid-back, clear, encouraging, and generally a great teacher on top of being an accomplished competitor. If you are focused on mid-peninsula competition no gi jiu jitsu, 10p SM is the place to go.

For my own part, I ended up reluctantly canceling my membership at 10p SM. This is for two main reasons: 1.) a major injury that I suffered, and how it was handled, and 2.) recurring difficulties with the owner, Adam Sachnoff. I wish I'd known about these issues before getting locked into a contract, so that's why I feel compelled to share my experience with you.

First, the story of my injury: about two months into training at 10p SM, my MCL popped so loud people could hear it across the room. I would not be fully healed for four months. That day, I had just submitted my fellow white belt training partner, and rather than slapping hands and rolling again, he got mad. He angrily flung my legs in an awkward, nonsensical direction, and my knee popped. The instructor, rather than setting the tone against such outbursts, had been on his phone the entire time (as was his habit) and did not raise his head even as the much of the class gathered in concern.

I approached the instructors afterwards to see if any good could come from debriefing the incident. Their attitude was, "Sorry, injuries happen in jiu jitsu". Of course that's true to some extent, but it doesn't mean that it's ok to have sloppy revenge injuries in an unsupervised class of white belts. Nevertheless, they didn't change anything, or even say a brief "let's try to be more careful" to the class. As a cherry on top, they went on to promote the perpetrator while I was still out injured.

The most significant issues I ran into with Adam revolved around COVID safety. I have a PhD in Epidemiology and wanted to help the gym, so I approached Adam about donating my time to improve our setup. Nothing that I suggested imposed costs on the gym. If we needed to buy something, I always offered to buy it myself and provide it to the gym for free.

Surprisingly, Adam was not willing to make any changes. He would not allow students to organize into a masks-only training pod. He would not ask the instructors to wear masks to decrease spread between pods. He would not deviate at all from his original plan, which included such knowledgeable attention to detail as "tempature checks" upon entering the gym's "loby". For good measure, he deleted my post on the team page about the benefit of masks.

Later on, I approached Adam again, hoping that a small group of us could train in the gym during off-hours. His conditions for this were that 1.) our masked group had to share the mat with an unmasked group, 2.) we could not bring in fans for ventilation or air filtration, 3.) we would have to pay the full membership price despite not having access to classes. When I said this wouldn't work for me, Adam suggested I train at a different gym.

At this point, I asked Adam for a refund of my remaining training balance so I could pay the fees at the new gym. At first, Adam told me that the money was non-refundable. There was no support for this in the contract. When I politely asked him to consider the many ways his rejection would not hold up, he abruptly agreed to write a check for the requested amount "ASAP". As a final and fitting note, Adam later asked that we chat for 5 minutes before he mailed the check. Rather than trying to end things on a positive note, it turns out that he was trying to negotiate me down on the amount that he had already willingly agreed to in writing. I had discounted over $500 already, so ultimately Adam agreed the requested amount was more than fair, and he issued the refund. He then quietly unfriended me on Facebook.</text>

<review>Before I joined 10th Planet San Mateo I researched a couple of gyms. Most didn't offer a warm up, and dove right into the technique. The instructor stood around after not really doing much. Then I discovered 10th Planet. Not only do we have a warm up for the body, but we also have warm ups for the technique which are super important for a sport like jiujitsu. What impressed me the most is the level of instruction Adam provides. He breaks down techniques to their core, explain's why they work, and how to counter those same techniques! In other gyms you simply drill the technique and if you're lucky you'll get a little theory as to why they work. I think the most valuable aspect of Adam's teaching is how he builds on a technique. We spend an entire month on a technique so that it gets into our muscle memory. No we don't drill the same "move" all month long. What we do is build from that move, say back takes, we drill an aspect of the back take one week, and . then move to a different aspect the next. And unlike other gyms where the instructor does nothing, Adam and the other coaches go around and actually help you out with the  techniques. The give you instant feedback and instant correction. If you've never done any time of martial arts don't worry! At 10th Planet San Mateo, they break down the class into sections - intro, beginner, advance. You'll be well taken care of. No matter what your goal is, compete, get in shape, self-defense etc. 10th Planet San Mateo and the high quality instruction will help you meet them!

I have to say that as one of the smaller females in the gym, I have never felt so safe training. I've trained at other gyms before, but the physical safety and secure I've experience here keeps me coming back. That and the friendships I've built with everyone. Come give us a try!< /review></record>

<review>So, since I always end up thinking too much and rewrite my words until I end up with an blank page again, which isn't very helpful for reviews, I'll go with a stream of consciousness approach.  Get ready for words...

It's taken some time to recognize the different ways that jiu jitsu has impacted my life, and I think the main reason for that, and why it seems so difficult to put into words, is because of how much it changed.  I barely recognize the person I was before starting jiu jitsu.  It has made me feel comfortable being inside my own body, mentally and physically.

I started out at the recommendation of my wife after being frustrated with being unable to manage it through time at the gym alone (also, I hated going to the gym).  I was vaguely aware of what jiu jitsu was before attending my first class, but the main appeal was that it was something different, and that there was no striking involved.  I had never done a forward roll before, let alone a backwards one, and I had never even thought about learning how to break my fall, or how to then stand up in a technically correct way.  How did I get up from the floor before?  Probably pretty awkwardly.  It also made me realize just how completely helpless and incapable I was at defending myself, even in a controlled environment.  How are you supposed to escape from a person that is on top of you?

Practicing self defense was never the intention, but neither was meeting new people.  I had no idea of the extended community I was joining and how welcoming it would turn out to be.  While going to the gym I might be surrounded by random people, here didn't have that same uncomfortable feeling.  Not that I would be remembering many names for a while, but there was more of a sense of camaraderie in knowing that everyone was once where I was, and that they were there to help guide me through motions that I didn't yet know I was capable of making.  Learning how to do things less badly slowly over time, Adam and the other instructors were always there to make adjustments during training and offer support and feedback along the way.

I can't imagine not doing jiu jitsu at this point.  Now a few years later, having to scramble and move because otherwise I'm going to be trapped underneath the big guy has enabled me to surpass my physical fitness goals (dropping from 225 to 185), but more often it just helps as a form of stress relief and mental reset--which might seem strange, but when being choked with only a few seconds of consciousness left, things are put into a clearer perspective.<//review>< Pictures>
None</Pictures>

If anything I wish I had more time during the week to dedicate to training. My experience so far has been fantastic. I came to 10th planet with no significant martial arts background and for someone like me learning BJJ can be intimidating and overwhelming at first. But, the instructors and the students at 10th Planet have all been welcoming, patient, encouraging, and friendly. Each session I learn something new, improve, struggle, get humbled, gain confidence, gain fitness, gain flexibility, and leave wanting more! It might not be for everyone in the end, but if you are interested in BJJ and looking for a great place to train with great people I'd highly recommend 10th Planet San Mateo.< /Text>< UserId.>

<Text>This is my second BJJ school. It works good for me for different reasons. 1. Week long theme in technique. I have chance to remember and drill through details (I'm not a gifted grappler and it take time for me). 2. Techiques usually taught in pairs with counter. This is great for trying it in rolls. 3. Situational sparring from position being drilled to try apply it in practice. 4. Open mat with practically unlimited rolls after class. 5. No gi. I like no gi much better, because it is dynamic. 6. Adam has assistants, higher belts, that look after student and ready explain, answer question or fix you. Definitely worth checking out.</Text><rating>5</rating>< UserId.>

<userid>114450732640065997153</userid>< Text>
10th Planet Jiu-Jitsu is HANDS DOWN the BEST gym in the Peninsula!!!!! Head Instructor, Adam "Big Red" Sachnoff, is a not only a highly decorated competitor (having one a gold medal at the International Brazilian Jiu-Jitsu Federation's World Championship amongst many other prestigious tournament wins) but also a GREAT teacher. He is really nice, funny, approachable, and easy going so he is awesome with complete beginners as well as advanced jiu-jitsu students; he is also a really good instructor to children as the kids' program is doing very well. Adam has a way of communicating details to EVERYONE so that no one is lost during class.

You won't find a better training environment in any other gym as EVERYONE is very friendly and welcoming of all those who come in. It is a  perfect gym for literally ALL WALKS OF LIFE. It doesn't matter if you're old, over-weight, out of shape, or any combination of the 3; it doesn't matter if you're a collegiate athlete in phenomenal shape; it doesn't matter if you're a man or a woman: this gym accommodates EVERYONE with all sorts of backgrounds.

No matter what you're looking for in jiu-jitsu you will find it here. If you want a fun and challenging way to get in shape rather than just running on a treadmill and/or lifting you should definitely try it out. If you're looking to compete in jiu-jitsu tournaments you should definitely check it out as the competition team is FIERCE.

Regardless of why you want to try jiu-jitsu and what you're looking to get out of it you will definitely find it at 10th Planet San Mateo!</Text>

< review>
The last thing you want to worry about when you lose a loved one is dealing with insurance companies, finances, burials, etc.  I called Evans-Brown Mortuary during some very tough times.  Carrie answered my call.  She was kind, answered all my concerns / questions and set up a meeting with me for the very next day.  During the meeting, she basically walked me through everything, taking her time, while making sure I was satisfied with the services they would be providing.  Their services were professionally done, on time and exactly as was described to me during the initial meeting. Days after, I received texts messages from Elizabeth and Carrie, simply to ask how I was doing and if there was anything else they could do.  With all the people they help on a daily, I thought sending a random text message just to check on how I was doing went far and beyond their job requirement.  I would recommend Evans-Brown Mortuary without hesitation.</review>

<userid>100797189144717426582</userid><Gmap_id>0x808fccfc95987603:0x564bb31e5e5c7ee2</Gmap_id><Pictures>None</Pictures>< response>
None< /response>
< text>
It's one of the best local pizza joints around but it could be THE best. I've been eating this pizza since I was in the womb. Anyone remember when the Old Italian owner would hang out with patrons? Autographed 49er memorabilia on the wall. The Green Parrot was still open then. The place used to be packed. Music blasting, beer flowing, arcade room. Nostalgia. Combo was to die for!!! Juices soaked through the pizza box. Every bite was pure spicy chorizo bliss.
Then the owner passed and his daughter took over. You no longer saw the same faces baking. Renovations took place, flavor changed (price didn't). Corners were cut. Less sauce.
Yes, the dough is still sweet. The combo doesn't have that kick to it anymore. But I still consider it the King of Pizza.<//text>

This place is absolutely gorgeous and has a hipster vibe. It's super original and not like any other coffee house. <Gmap_id>0x80900d71bad2f289:0xdd621f51ee651b2b</Gmap_id><Review>Unfortunately, on the 1st day of my New Year, I had a pretty bad experience (once again mind you) at Empresso Coffeehouse. Let me first start off by saying I really think this place is cool. I like the array of events that happen there and the majority of people who frequent the spot seem to be artistic & peaceful. It's the customer service & attitude from certain staff members that is the problem. Not all of them....but certain ones for sure. I tend not to go to Empresso Coffeehouse so often anymore due to several other past incidents that happened there with staff but after a year or 2 hiatus from this place, I've recently tried to let bygones be bygones & started to visit the place once or twice a month again. But today's incident took the cake.....literally & just reenforced the reason why I stopped going there in the first place. I went in this place of business to purchase several pastries for me and my family to enjoy for New Year's. The cashier by the name of Tiffany was helping a white lady in front of me. The service she provided to the lady before me seemed to be pretty good & fair. But I immediately noticed a not so friendly vibe from Tiffany once it was my turn for assistance. Maybe she's having a bad day or a hang over from last night's New Year's festivities but whatever it is, she seemed to be not so friendly specifically towards me. I overlooked her unfriendly demeanor and waited....& waited for her to at least say hello or how can I help you. After about 30-45 uncomfortable seconds of me standing right in front of her while she acted as if she didn't see me there, she finally looked up and says "Do you need something?"  I brushed that off as well and told her yes while pointing to the piece of pastry that I wanted. She looked at the pastry as if she was frustrated, then asked, "Is that all you want?". I told her that I'd like to order several more pastries as well. After she sighed & acted like she was doing me a favor by dragging herself to the back room to get a box to place the pastries in, she came back and started picking pieces other than what I had asked for. I reiterated that I wanted the particular pieces that I asked for. She began to argue with me saying all the pieces were the same. Even though they were not all the same, I asked if all the pieces are the same, why can't I choose the piece that I want? She began to tell me how she can't choose one piece over another & how they have to pick a certain piece and blah blah blah.....it didn't make a bit of sense. I tried to brush it off again and asked her to please give me what I'm paying for and she was absolutely reluctant in providing me with what I asked for. I then asked for her manger and she informed that Empresso Coffeehouse does not have a manager. Found that strange as well. Then I asked who is the owner. She told me his name is Troy but he can not be contacted for blah blah blah reasons....once again....made no sense. I immediately turned and left the building. I have since obtained Troy's full name (Troy Burke), email, Facebook, etc....and messaged him about this incident. I truly hope he or someone who acts as some sort of management for this place responds or contacts me soon in regards to this extremely poor & unacceptable customer service being directed towards a paying customer that would actually like to frequent this place business. I'm not sure why she acted this way & I don't want to make any assumptions that seem to be part of the reason why because I don't want to believe in hate to that degree in a place of business like this but......until I am contacted, I have no choice but to go back to my previous sentiments about Empresso Coffeehouse & take my money elsewhere. Please learn how to treat all customers the same regardless of race, gender, if you're having a bad day, etc...etc.... Your paying customers deserve that. Happy New Year!

UPDATE: 1/6/2016
This is an update to my review since being contacted by the owner. He apologized & was extremely sincere & professional. I was informed all issues were addressed. Thank you!< /Review><Response>None< /Response>< UserId.>

< userid>
114801194004846977680</userid>
< username>
Vit√≥rio Ferrinezza< /username>
<Time>1423453224639</Time>< rate>
4</rate>
<text>It's not Peets but it is Stockton and a reminder that as long as you don't give up on a city...good things can happen.

When I lived in Stockton in the 80s,  I often said that if the Royal went down, the place would make a great little coffee concept. My vision was a little more upscale, a little closer to Berkeleyesque but still maintaining a funk that few places could provide without being run by air cooled engine enthusiasts. Bravo Stockton for supporting such a place and bravo to ownership for providing the space.

As for the coffee, not bad. The house coffee is often just on the cusp of hitting the shelf life which is normal for indies......you'll know by the coffee having that initial hit immediately followed by thought of what if I simply add sugar. The finish is bitter...any fragrance beaten into submission. Still, it does accomplish it's task of hitting you over the head into consciousness. And while a pastry might soften the blow, it only makes the coffee that much more difficult, even with a little extra cream. Some would argue that intensity and bitterness go Mano a Mano. ...not so gentle readers. Other suggest using sugar....sorry....coffee should not require sugar to have a balanced experience while the mouth is processing the initial consumption. Perhaps the roaster took a few extra minutes taking that restroom break during the most critical period of the roasting process or perhaps not enough time was given to the mellowing of the beans after roasting. Personally I favor roasting beans on site if for no other reason that the aroma carries for miles and coffee freaks follow the scent to the source and statistically consume an extra cup per visit......important if you charge for refills. Still, simply brewing a new pot on a more established and consistent time table is often the simple solution.

Service meets expectations. Decora could stand less dust though not a complete sterilization as that would impinge on the funk factor. Outdoor seating is a nice touch. ....no bullet proof vests needed. Nice view of other nice establishments worthy of inspection. In fact the Miracle Mile is the gem of Stockton in my view. Parking is good enough during peak periods unless your longest stretch is from your bed to kitchen to toilet every day.

Yes....Stockton is good people.</text>< Pics>
None</Pics>
